     move the gate to root. -->

## [Unreleased]
### Added
- **Dashboard surface for the North Mini Code coding brain** (2026-07-18). The North default + interleaved-thinking control shipped backend-only, so nothing was visible in the UI. The `/api/doctor` report — which the v5 **Doctor** screen renders generically — now includes a **"Coding brain (North Mini Code)"** check under the `Models` category showing the active coding/executor model, whether `NORTH_MINI_CODE_DEFAULT` is on, and the interleaved-thinking setting (`OLLAMA_REASONING_EFFORT`, or Ollama's auto-default). It reports `pass` in normal configs (North on Ollama/OpenRouter, or the expected NVIDIA-only-production fallback) and `warn` only when an operator has switched the default off. Hermes runtime health is already surfaced as a `Runtime` check on the same screen, so the two now sit side-by-side. Read-only, defensive (never breaks the report). Files: `backend/server.py`, `tests/test_doctor_coding_brain.py` (2 tests).

### Fixed
- **"Set default" on the Providers page 500'd unconditionally — default provider could never change from DeepSeek** (2026-07-19). Root cause confirmed via screenshot + direct repro: `packages/storage/sqlite.py`'s `_Collection` class — the Motor-compatible adapter `STORAGE_BACKEND=sqlite` production uses — had no `update_many()` method at all. `backend/server.py`'s `create_provider()`/`update_provider()` call `providers.update_many({"provider_id": {"$ne": id}}, {"$set": {"is_default": False}})` to clear every other provider's flag before setting the new default; on sqlite this raised a bare `AttributeError` on every single call, not just under transient load, which is why the default was stuck on whatever was seeded at startup (DeepSeek) no matter which provider's "Set default" button was clicked, and why the error was the literal `"Request failed with status code 500"` shown directly on the Providers page. Added `update_many()` to `_Collection` (applies `$set`/`$push`/`$inc` etc. to every matching row, mirroring `update_one`'s per-doc `_apply_update` and `delete_many`'s all-matches iteration). Also hardened `create_provider`/`update_provider`/`delete_provider` and the related `GET /api/providers/{id}/models` (which had the same unguarded-DB-call shape and 500'd on switching the Brain Card to a provider like Moonshot that has no `providers` collection row) to fail with a clear `503` or fall back to the predefined model catalog instead of an opaque 500. Files: `packages/storage/sqlite.py`, `backend/server.py`, `tests/test_sqlite_store.py` (3 tests), `tests/test_provider_models_db_outage.py` (3 tests).
- **Company onboarding wizard's "Connect your resources" step 500'd when saving a GitHub access token** (2026-07-19). `PUT /api/github/token` (and `DELETE /api/github/token`) built the Mongo update filter with a bare `ObjectId(uid)`. On the production Render deployment (`STORAGE_BACKEND=sqlite`) — and for the env-admin fallback user `get_optional_user()` constructs when the DB is briefly unreachable (`_id="admin_user_001"`) — the authenticated user's `_id` is a plain string, not a valid Mongo ObjectId hex string, so `ObjectId()` raised an uncaught `bson.errors.InvalidId` that FastAPI turned into a bare 500 with no `detail` body. The frontend onboarding wizard (`DetailsStep` in `OnboardingScreen.jsx`) surfaced this as axios's generic `"Request failed with status code 500"` right after entering a GitHub token and clicking Continue, blocking onboarding entirely for any SQLite-backed or DB-degraded admin session. New `_user_id_filter()` helper tries `ObjectId(uid)` and falls back to the raw string, mirroring the existing ObjectId-then-string retry already used in `get_optional_user()`; both endpoints now use it. Files: `backend/server.py`, `tests/test_github_token_regression.py` (2 tests).
- **Changelog corruption cleaned up + parity gate hardened to reject it at the source** (2026-07-18). The root `CHANGELOG.md` and `docs/changelog.md` had accumulated a duplicate `## [Unreleased]` heading (and, in earlier PRs, leftover git-conflict/stash markers) that kept riding through CI silently — `check_changelog_parity.py::_blocks` keys sections by version and lets the *last* `## [X]` win, so a second `[Unreleased]` masked real content drift and forced a manual conflict resolution on PRs #1071 and #1076. Merged the two `[Unreleased]` sections into one and re-synced `docs/changelog.md` to the canonical root file (parity now compares the whole section, not just the last heading). New `scan_corruption()` in `scripts/check_changelog_parity.py` fails the gate (exit 2) on any conflict/stash marker or duplicate version heading, so this can't recur unnoticed. Files: `CHANGELOG.md`, `docs/changelog.md`, `scripts/check_changelog_parity.py`, `tests/test_changelog_parity_guard.py` (6 tests).
- **Cross-machine local-brain daemon hit `/v1/v1/models` (double `/v1`) on every probe — silently misread a live brain as dead** (2026-07-17). `scripts/local_controller.py`'s `_probe_v1_models()` appends `/v1/models` to whatever `base_url` it is handed, so any caller that ALSO passed `/v1` produced an invalid request that local openai-compatible servers (colibri, llama-server.exe, ollama, kimi-local-llama) answered with `404` (or `URLError`). The daemon's heartbeat then reported `port_state=dead` even while the brain was actually serving, which is why the cross-machine Providers toggle kept showing a falsely-red status pill on the Cloudflare-deployed admin SPA. Dropped the redundant `/v1` suffix at all four call sites (`_choose_local_brain` line 165, readiness loop ~487, restart re-probe ~531, `--diagnose` mode ~599); post-fix the probe URL is `http://127.0.0.1:{port}/v1/models` (single `/v1`) and a brain that was secretly answering the wrong path now flips the dashboard green without operator action. Operator may see a sudden red-to-green on their wall — read that as the fix, not a regression. While here, also deleted the redundant `_probe_v1_models(base_local)` probe that double-set `currently_running` after `_choose_local_brain` already returned it (saves one HTTP probe per tick), and locked the readiness / restart / restart-else probes to `http_port` directly (saves ~1,200 ping-pong probes during a 40-minute cold load between colibri slow path :8081 and the engine we just started :8072). Test coverage: 3 tests rewritten in `tests/test_local_controller.py` (strict-URL exact-sequence assertion, renamed `restart_reprobes_http_port_only`, leaf-stub rewrite of `picks_colibri_8081_when_only_it_listening`); new `_fake_http_sequence` helper yields the recorded urlopen call list so any future re-introduction of an extra probe (or any /v1 regression) fails loudly. Files: `scripts/local_controller.py`, `tests/test_local_controller.py`.
### Added

- **Explicit interleaved-thinking control for Ollama coding models (`OLLAMA_REASONING_EFFORT`)** (2026-07-18). North Mini Code "works best with thinking on", and on Ollama's OpenAI-compatible `/v1/chat/completions` endpoint the native `think: true` is ignored — the effort is controlled via `reasoning_effort` (`high`/`medium`/`low`). Ollama already auto-enables thinking for capable models (North Mini Code, deepseek-r1, qwen3) when it's omitted, so this is an opt-in control, not a behaviour change: the new `OLLAMA_REASONING_EFFORT` env (default unset) pins/forces the effort level. New shared helper `with_ollama_reasoning_effort()` in `packages/ai/router.py` injects the field for Ollama requests only (a no-op — returns the same object — for non-Ollama providers, when unset, or when the caller already set it), wired into both LLM request paths: the router chat path (`_post_chat`) and the agent loop's brain-failover executor path (`agent/loop.py`). Because the default is unset, every request is byte-for-byte unchanged unless an operator opts in. Files: `packages/config/settings.py`, `packages/ai/router.py`, `agent/loop.py`, `.env.example`, `tests/test_north_mini_code.py` (5 new tests). Note: end-to-end thinking output against a live Ollama-hosted North was not validated in CI (no GPU/model available); the unit tests cover the injection logic and the byte-identical default path. Also fixes a test-isolation regression surfaced by this PR: #1075's autouse `_isolate_brain_data_layer` conftest fixture stubbed `db.users.find_one → None`, which 401'd admin-login tests (e.g. `tests/test_activity_logs.py`) whose pytest collection order this PR's new test file shifted; the fixture now skips tests using the real `client` fixture (the `app_client`-based `test_brain_config_api.py` isolation it was added for is unaffected). File: `tests/conftest.py`.
- **North Mini Code 1.0 is the default agentic coding brain for the agency + Hermes** (2026-07-18). Integrated Cohere Labs' first open-weight code model — `north-mini-code-1.0`, a 30B/3B-active sparse-MoE (Apache-2.0, 256K context, native tool-use + interleaved thinking, RLVR-trained on real SWE/terminal tasks; SWE-bench Verified 67.6, Terminal-Bench 2.0 36.0) — as the default model for the agency's code-execution loop and every Hermes task, wherever the active provider can serve it. Wiring: the Ollama **executor** (code-writing) role preset is now `north-mini-code-1.0` and the OpenRouter executor preset is `cohere/north-mini-code:free` (`config/models.yaml` + the hardcoded mirror in `packages/ai/brain_config.py`); both ids are registered in `router/registry.py` (coder, 262K context, `cost_tier=2` so `best_model_for` still returns the existing heaviest-tier coder — no proxy-routing regression). New `resolve_coding_model_preference()` in `brain_config.py` returns North's id only when the `NORTH_MINI_CODE_DEFAULT` flag is on **and** the active provider (local Ollama / OpenRouter free) can actually serve it; it returns `None` on NVIDIA-only production, which `runtimes/adapters/internal_agent.py` (the path Hermes runs through) reads as "no override" so the normal per-role brain runs — North can never break a deployment that doesn't host it. A non-`None` value makes the whole plan→execute→verify loop run on North, its intended single-model agentic-harness usage. Switchable: `NORTH_MINI_CODE_DEFAULT=false` disables it, and the Brain card can switch the executor preset at any time. Because `call_llm` (SAM's path) resolves the provider `default_model`, SAM's general chat is unaffected. Files: `packages/config/settings.py`, `config/models.yaml`, `packages/ai/brain_config.py`, `router/registry.py`, `runtimes/adapters/internal_agent.py`, `.env.example`, `tests/test_north_mini_code.py` (11 tests), and updated the keyless-default assertions in `tests/test_unit7_catalog_propagation.py` and `tests/test_chat_mode_regressions.py` to North.
- **Richer, more readable Telegram approval-gate message** (2026-07-18). The "⏸ Task awaiting approval" notification was bare — task ID, title, and "tap a button" — giving an operator with several gated tasks in flight no way to tell them apart without opening the dashboard. `TaskExecutionCoordinator._notify_execution_gate` now includes a priority emoji (🔴 urgent / 🟠 high / 🟡 medium / 🟢 low), task type, owner (so system-generated tasks like `system:trend-scoping` are distinguishable from user-created ones), and a redacted/truncated description excerpt (reusing the same `_redact_for_notification` secret-scrubbing helper already used by the workflow-orchestrator's approval-gate message, so pasted secrets in a task description can't leak into Telegram). Also points the operator at the dashboard's Job Board "Awaiting approval" banner (added in the dashboard-surface fix above) as an alternative to the inline buttons. Files: `tasks/service.py`, `tests/test_telegram_gate_message_format.py` (3 tests).

- **Dashboard surface for the pre-execution approval gate** (2026-07-17). The "⏸ Task awaiting approval" Telegram notification told operators to approve "via the dashboard", but the dashboard had no such surface: nothing in the frontend called `POST /api/tasks/{id}/approve-execution`, and a parked system-owned task (e.g. trend scoping's `system:trend-scoping`) was invisible on the Job Board because `GET /api/tasks/` returns only the 50 newest tasks for the caller (owner-scoped for non-admins). New `GET /api/tasks/awaiting-approval` endpoint returns every task parked at the gate (admins see all owners, non-admins their own), and the v5 Job Board now shows an "Awaiting approval before execution" banner with working ✓ Approve / ✕ Reject buttons wired to `approve-execution`. Files: `tasks/store.py` (`list_awaiting_approval`), `tasks/api.py`, `frontend/src/api.js`, `frontend/src/v5/screens/TaskBoardScreen.jsx`, `tests/test_tasks_awaiting_approval_api.py` (4 tests).

- **Local brain pivoted to on-disk `qwen2.5-coder-7b-instruct-q4_k_m.gguf` (4.36 GB) on this operator machine** (2026-07-17). The earlier "GLM-5.2 local brain" thread assumed `openai/glm-5.2` on Hugging Face, which the HF API returns `404 - Repository Not Found` for - no such model is published there. The locally-on-disk qwen2.5-coder GGUF at D:\hfkld-qg7ky\local-models\gguf\qwen2.5-coder-7b-instruct-q4_k_m.gguf (Q4_K_M 4.36 GB) now powers the cross-machine toggle: llama-server.exe on 127.0.0.1:8072 with BRAIN_PREFERENCE=local-brain, LOCAL_BRAIN_MODEL_PATH / LOCAL_BRAIN_MODEL_ID / LOCAL_BRAIN_CTX=4096 so the 4 GB weights + 4 GB KV cache fit comfortably in the 8 GB iGPU budget. Cloud brain remains z-ai/glm-5.2 on NVIDIA NIM (build.nvidia.com/z-ai/glm-5.2) for all non-local routes. The 360 GB D:\hfkld-qg7ky\local-models\GLM-5.2\ orphan dir (stray .safetensors from a much earlier broken python -m attempt) has been reclaimed. Files: .env.example, docs/changelog.md. Note: JustVugg/colibri C engine is still cloned at D:\hfkld-qg7ky\local-models\colibri\; once a real GLM-5.x release lands on HF (or a different GGUF candidate is on disk), the same BRAIN_PREFERENCE=local-brain + LOCAL_BRAIN_MODEL_PATH switch surfaces it no .py/.jsx changes required.

### Fixed
- **Production storage switched from ephemeral SQLite to MongoDB (`render.yaml`)** (2026-07-18). `/api/health` on the live Render service reported `"backend":"sqlite"` — but Render's disk is ephemeral, so the entire task store (tasks, agents, history) was silently wiped on every deploy; this is how the parked trend task vanished from the dashboard while a stale local Docker stack kept its own copy alive. `STORAGE_BACKEND` in `render.yaml` now reads `mongo` for the web service (matching the documented production architecture in CLAUDE.md). Also fixed `local-llm-server-worker` (CodeRabbit review on this PR): it runs its own `TaskDispatcher` (`worker_main.py`) and had `MONGO_URL` already provisioned but `STORAGE_BACKEND` left at `sqlite` — a second, independent split-brain (this worker dispatching against its own ephemeral file, invisible to the web service). Left `agency-hermes` and `freebuff-telegram-bot` on sqlite/no-Mongo: verified neither touches the task store (`services/hermes_server.py` is a pure sandboxed code-exec runtime; `scripts/run_freebuff_bot.py` runs FreeBuff in embedded mode by design — "no MongoDB" — with `TELEGRAM_POLLER_DISABLED=true` by default so it doesn't even handle approval callbacks). DEPLOY PREREQUISITE: `MONGO_URL` (Atlas connection string) must be set in the Render dashboard for both `local-llm-server` and `local-llm-server-worker` before this deploys — `packages/storage/mongo.py` falls back to `mongodb://localhost:27017` when unset, which does not exist on Render. Files: `render.yaml`.

- **Approval-gate Telegram notification re-sent every ~5 minutes for the same parked task** (2026-07-18). The reconciler's second pass re-queued every TODO task with `pending_agent_run=False` — but that is exactly how the pre-execution gate parks a `requires_approval` task. Cycle: gate parks + notifies -> reconciler re-arms -> dispatcher re-picks -> gate re-parks + re-notifies, on every reconcile cycle (~5 min at the default `TASK_RECONCILE_EVERY_POLLS=60` x 5 s poll, plus every server restart) until a human decided. Two-part fix: (1) `tasks/store.py` — the reconciler's unqueued-TODO pass now skips tasks with `requires_approval` set and `execution_approved` unset, so gate-parked tasks stay parked; (2) `tasks/service.py` — the gate only sends the Telegram notification on the FIRST park (no prior `approval_gate` event in the execution log), so any future re-arm path cannot spam. Regression suite `tests/test_reconciler_respects_approval_gate.py` (2 tests) fails against the pre-fix code. Files: `tasks/store.py`, `tasks/service.py`, `tests/test_reconciler_respects_approval_gate.py`.
- `.env.example`: restore 6 missing backslashes on `LOCAL_BRAIN_MODEL_PATH` (sed escape in a prior session ate them) AND drop the stale `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri` example line in the brain-preference selector (colibri never built; live brain path is `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=local-brain` via `:8072`).

- **Cross-machine local-brain daemon hit `/v1/v1/models` (double `/v1`) on every probe — silently misread a live brain as dead** (2026-07-17). `scripts/local_controller.py`'s `_probe_v1_models()` appends `/v1/models` to whatever `base_url` it is handed, so any caller that ALSO passed `/v1` produced an invalid request that local openai-compatible servers (colibri, llama-server.exe, ollama, kimi-local-llama) answered with `404` (or `URLError`). The daemon's heartbeat then reported `port_state=dead` even while the brain was actually serving, which is why the cross-machine Providers toggle kept showing a falsely-red status pill on the Cloudflare-deployed admin SPA. Dropped the redundant `/v1` suffix at all four call sites (`_choose_local_brain` line 165, readiness loop ~487, restart re-probe ~531, `--diagnose` mode ~599); post-fix the probe URL is `http://127.0.0.1:{port}/v1/models` (single `/v1`) and a brain that was secretly answering the wrong path now flips the dashboard green without operator action. Operator may see a sudden red-to-green on their wall — read that as the fix, not a regression. While here, also deleted the redundant `_probe_v1_models(base_local)` probe that double-set `currently_running` after `_choose_local_brain` already returned it (saves one HTTP probe per tick), and locked the readiness / restart / restart-else probes to `http_port` directly (saves ~1,200 ping-pong probes during a 40-minute cold load between colibri slow path :8081 and the engine we just started :8072). Test coverage: 3 tests rewritten in `tests/test_local_controller.py` (strict-URL exact-sequence assertion, renamed `restart_reprobes_http_port_only`, leaf-stub rewrite of `picks_colibri_8081_when_only_it_listening`); new `_fake_http_sequence` helper yields the recorded urlopen call list so any future re-introduction of an extra probe (or any /v1 regression) fails loudly. Files: `scripts/local_controller.py`, `tests/test_local_controller.py`.

- **Telegram task-approval Approve/Reject buttons errored and never saved the decision** (2026-07-17). The `requires_approval` gate notification gained inline Approve/Reject buttons, but `telegram_bot.py`'s `_process_task_callback` called `await workflow.approve_execution(...)` even though `TaskWorkflowService.approve_execution` is synchronous — awaiting its `Task` return value raised `TypeError: object Task can't be used in 'await' expression` *before* the store update, so tapping a button showed an error toast and the task stayed parked. Removed the two erroneous `await`s: ✅ Approve now sets `execution_approved`, re-queues the task (`pending_agent_run=True`, status IN_PROGRESS — the dispatcher's `list_pending` scan picks it up) and edits the Telegram message to “Approved”; ❌ Reject blocks the task with the reason recorded. New regression suite `tests/test_telegram_task_callback.py` (4 tests) drives `_process_task_callback` end-to-end against an in-memory store — it fails against the pre-fix code. Files: `telegram_bot.py`, `tests/test_telegram_task_callback.py`.

### Added
- **Build script for llama-server.exe (cross-machine GLM-5.2 brain)** (2026-07-16). New `scripts/build_llama_cpp.ps1` (~210 LOC, idempotent, MSVC + CMake) clones llama.cpp with `--depth 1` and produces `llama-server.exe` at the default `D:\hfkld-qg7ky\local-models\llama.cpp\build\bin\Release\llama-server.exe` (overridable via `-LlamaCppDir`). Closes the missing-binary gap that blocks `scripts/local_controller.py` (cross-machine toggle daemon) from spawning inference when the Cloudflare-deployed Providers page flips the Local brain toggle ON. Prereq probes (git + cmake + `where.exe cl.exe >NUL`) fast-fail with operator-friendly install guidance; nvcc absence auto-fallbacks to CPU-only. Logs to `logs/build-llama-cpp.log`; exit codes 0-5 with clear failure modes.
- **Default boot path is now colibri (JustVugg/colibri GLM-5.2 744B MoE) brain watchdog, not Ollama** (2026-07-16). Per operator direction — "remove the ollama service on start up and do the colibri service start instead". `start_server.ps1` Step 1 now launches `python scripts/monitor_colibri.py supervise` (with a 6-iter `/v1/models` readiness probe that never `exit 1`s so slow model loads don't abort the boot sequence) instead of `run_ollama.bat`. The previously-conditional Step 4 colibri block is gone (it's now in Step 1, unconditional). PID map drops the `ollama` key. `setup_autostart.ps1` Task Scheduler entry renamed `Qwen3-Coder-Server` -> `Colibri-GLM-5.2-Server` with description updated. Ollama remains available as a fallback brain (ops set `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=ollama` and run `run_ollama.bat` manually); brain_policy.py / packages/ai/brain.py still understand `ollama`. NOTE: colibri :8081 doesn't bind today (JustVugg upstream `c/openai_server.py:442` `Popen([executable, cap])` drops `--model --port --host`; 383 GB weights > 128 GB RAM is hardware-fatal). The watchdog retries forever until upstream is patched or hardware is upgraded; see `NEXT_ACTION.md` for the path forward. Files: `start_server.ps1`, `setup_autostart.ps1`.
- **Fixed silent `env_ollama` fallback when `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri` is set** (2026-07-16). Local `.env` had `COLIBRI_LOCAL_LLAMA_URL` (legacy/typo'd key) but **`packages/ai/brain.py:354` + `providers/colibri.py:52,71` + `scripts/monitor_lib.py:79` + `start_tunnel.py:45`** all read the **canonical** name `COLIBRI_URL`. The resolver's loud warning ("`BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri but COLIBRI_URL is unset`") was firing but no live brain picks up logs — so the resolver silently fell through to `ollama_local` + `qwen3-coder:30b`. Added `COLIBRI_URL=http://localhost:8081/v1` and `COLIBRI_MODEL=glm-5.2` to local `.env` (canonical names; legacy `COLIBRI_LOCAL_LLAMA_*` keys kept for backward compat). Post-fix, `brain.resolve_active_brain()` returns `provider_id='colibri', source='env_colibri', priority=100` so the operator's local GLM-5.2 intent is honored. NOTE: colibri :8081 itself still doesn't bind (see above) — the resolver now ROUTES to colibri intent, the watchdog retries until binding works. Files: `.env` (local-only, git-ignored); committed knowledge lives in `.env.example` lines 302–303.
- Admin-session-gated `/admin/api/local-brain/{state,toggle}` proxy so the
  Cloudflare-deployed admin SPA (Providers page) can flip the local
  GLM-5.2 brain toggle without ever touching the SERVICE_TOKEN secret.
  Same body shape as the existing SERVICE_TOKEN routes so the React
  `LocalBrainToggleCard` component needs zero JS edits; auth via the
  existing admin JWT session. The SERVICE_TOKEN-gated `/api/local-brain/heartbeat`
  path is unchanged (still required for the local daemon on the operator
  machine).
  - **Cross-machine GLM-5.2 brain toggle** (2026-07-15). Operator-facing button on the Cloudflare-deployed Providers page that starts/stops the local llama-server.exe serving GLM-5.2 on the operator machine (or any local box with the setup) when toggled on, and lets the brain fall back to the cloud recommended chain (NVIDIA -> Cerebras -> Groq) when toggled off. Wired end-to-end: backend/local_brain_router.py (3 endpoints gated on SERVICE_TOKEN; SQLite-persisted via backend/local_brain_store.py); frontend/src/v5/components/LocalBrainToggleCard.jsx (status pill + Start/Stop + heartbeat payload viewer, mounted under BrainCard on ProvidersScreen); scripts/local_controller.py (pull-based daemon polling every 30s); scripts/start_local_glm_server.ps1 + scripts/stop_local_glm_server.ps1 + scripts/setup_local_controller.ps1 (Windows launcher with PID lock + Task Scheduler AtStartup/AtLogon autostart). Reviewer-vetted: lease TTL = 90s after last healthy heartbeat (no stale lockout), non-blocking cold start (heartbeat during 240s load), PowerShell BOM bug fixed (System.IO.File.WriteAllText ASCII encoding so cmd.exe parses the wrapper.cmd cleanly). Files: backend/local_brain_router.py, backend/local_brain_store.py, scripts/local_controller.py, scripts/start_local_glm_server.ps1, scripts/stop_local_glm_server.ps1, scripts/setup_local_controller.ps1, frontend/src/v5/components/LocalBrainToggleCard.jsx, tests/test_local_brain_state.py, tests/test_local_controller.py.
- **Colibri brain-shim regression gate - `tests/test_colibri_brain_shim.py`** (2026-07-15). Pins the `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri` env-shim (wired by commits f5ee801 + 134db80) as a CI trip-wire so any future rip-out from `brain_policy` / `provider_router` / `scripts/switch_brain.py` fails the gate. Covers the allowlist, `/v1` URL normalization (including trailing-slash idempotence), `COLIBRI_MODEL` defaults + `AGENT_LLM_MODEL` fallback, the loud warning on missing `COLIBRI_URL`, the records-bypass (a stale DB record must not preempt operator intent), and the free-NVIDIA bypass-guard when `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri` is set alongside `NVIDIA_API_KEY`. Introduced in PR #1052. Files: `tests/test_colibri_brain_shim.py`.
- **Colibri brain-shim regression gate - `tests/test_colibri_brain_shim.py`** (2026-07-15). CI trip-wire for the BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri wiring installed in commits f5ee801 + 134db80 + PR #1050. Pins the env-shim so any future rip-out (kimi-style leftover, colibri dropping out of valid set, stale DB record preempting operator intent, free-NVIDIA bypass-guard regressing when NVIDIA_API_KEY is set) trips at CI time. - **Post-HF-download monitor stack for the colibri + GLM-5.2 brain** (2026-07-14). Bridges the gap between an in-flight 370 GB `hf download` of the GLM-5.2 weights and the local colibri inference server actually answering inference. Four-piece surface: (1) **`scripts/monitor_lib.py`** — pure std-lib helpers (`download_status()` distinguishing in-progress / stalled / done / missing-dir / no-log; `await_ready()` blocking probe on `/v1/models` with bounded timeout, injective retries, optional model-id match; `is_process_alive()` cross-platform PID check via `tasklist` on Windows + `os.kill(0)` elsewhere; `supervise_tick()` state machine returning one of {heartbeat, crash-restart, manual-stop, adopted}; `write_supervisor_state()` atomic temp-file + rename so power loss mid-write cannot corrupt the state). (2) **`scripts/monitor_colibri.py`** — CLI entrypoint with subcommands: `status` (one-shot JSON snapshot of download + server + supervisor), `wait` (block until both download AND `/v1/models` report ready, default 12 h timeout), `supervise` (long-running watchdog; exponential backoff 4 s → 300 s capped at 5 consecutive crashes; **deliberately does NOT auto-restart when `.colibri.pid` is absent** so an operator's deliberate `stop_colibri_server.ps1` is respected), `autostart-install` (idempotent Task Scheduler wrapper). (3) **`scripts/wait_for_colibri_ready.ps1`** + **`scripts/setup_monitor_autostart.ps1`** — PowerShell wrappers; the autostart script registers `ColibriMonitor` with `AtStartup` + `AtLogOn` triggers as session 0 SYSTEM and is **idempotent** (drops the prior task before re-registering, never accumulates dupes). `start_server.ps1` gains a conditional `[4/4]` step that launches the supervisor in background iff `BRAIN_PREFERENCE=colibri`. (4) Comprehensive test coverage in **`tests/test_monitor_lib.py`** — download status matrix, readiness probe (success / retries / timeout / 503 / no-model-id), PID-file parsing (missing / valid / malformed / whitespace), process liveness via mocked `tasklist`, supervisor tick for all four states + atomic state-file writes + corrupt-recovery + give-up-after-max-crashes. **State files** in `D:\hfkld-qg7ky\local-models\colibri\`: `.colibri.pid` (PID, removed by stop script), `.colibri.supervisor.state` (crash counter + timestamps, atomic write), `.colibri.monitor.log` (heartbeats). All paths env-overridable via `COLIBRI_DIR` / `COLIBRI_MODEL_DIR` / `COLIBRI_DOWNLOAD_LOG` / `COLIBRI_URL` / `COLIBRI_MODEL_ID` so the suite stays hermetic. Files: `scripts/monitor_lib.py`, `scripts/monitor_colibri.py`, `scripts/wait_for_colibri_ready.ps1`, `scripts/setup_monitor_autostart.ps1`, `tests/test_monitor_lib.py`, `start_server.ps1`, `.env.example`, `docs/changelog.md`.
- **Agent tasks with failed steps marked DONE - no follow-up, no self-heal, no PR** (2026-07-14). Tasks with 7/9 steps applied (2 failed with syntax errors) were marked DONE because the step-success-ratio gate was 50%. The 2 failed steps were silently dropped - the CEO never created a follow-up task, no PR was opened, and the agency went quiet. Fix: (1) Changed the step-success-ratio gate from 50% to 100% - ANY failed step now marks the task as FAILED so the CEO + self_heal can pick it up for retry. (2) Improved the syntax error feedback in _local_syntax_check - now includes the offending line + 2 lines of context with a >>> marker, so the LLM can see exactly what is wrong and fix it on retry instead of repeating the same mistake. - **CI red: npm ci fails (package-lock.json out of sync) — Cloudflare deploy, Playwright, Nightly Regression all fail** (2026-07-13). This broke: Cloudflare Worker deploy, Playwright browser tests (Dockerfile.backend builds the SPA via npm ci), and Nightly Regression (same Docker build). - **Fix sqlite adapter sort crash on mixed float/str timestamps** (2026-07-13). The `TaskDispatcher error: '<' not supported between instances of 'float' and 'str'` was caused by the sqlite adapter's `sort()` method in `packages/storage/sqlite.py`. When `STORAGE_BACKEND=sqlite` (the Render default), the TaskStore runs in 'mongo' mode using the sqlite adapter's collection API. The adapter's sort used `sorted(rows, key=lambda r: r.get(key) or "")` — when some rows have float `updated_at` and others have ISO 8601 string `updated_at`, the comparison crashes. Fixed all 3 sort spots (line 107 `_Cursor.__init__`, line 145 `_Cursor.sort`, line 595 `$sort` aggregate pipeline) with a new `_safe_sort_key()` helper that normalises any value to float before comparison.
- **Skip freebuff test in CI when no LLM is configured** (2026-07-13). `test_run_coerces_requested_model_to_free` in `tests/test_freebuff.py` requires a live LLM endpoint for the planning phase (before the mocked `AgentRunner.run` is called). In CI where no NVIDIA/Ollama endpoint is available, the test fails with `All brain providers exhausted`. Added a `@pytest.mark.skipif` guard that skips the test when neither `NVIDIA_API_KEY` nor `OLLAMA_BASE` is set.
- **Fix MCP test event loop crash on Python 3.13** (2026-07-13). `test_list_tools_passes_output_schema_through` in `tests/test_daily_automation_2026_07_13.py` used `asyncio.get_event_loop().run_until_complete(...)` which raises `RuntimeError: There is no current event loop` on Python 3.13. Switched to `asyncio.run(...)` which is the loop-state-independent replacement.

- **Stop mislabeling near-total step-failure as "Done" (3 confirmed bugs)** (2026-07-13). Two production tasks (task_530055f2c383c940: 1/22 steps applied; a portfolio_initiative: 1/10 steps applied) were marked DONE despite 95%+ step failure. Three separate, verifiable bugs caused this: (1) `runtimes/adapters/internal_agent.py:519` — `did_work` was True if ANY step was applied or any output >20 chars, regardless of how many steps failed. Fixed with a step-success-ratio gate: `steps_ok = step_success_ratio is None or step_success_ratio >= 0.5`. A task with planned steps now needs a MAJORITY applied to count as done; the free-text-report path only applies when there were NO steps (pure analysis tasks). (2) `agent/loop.py` — `run()`'s return dict never included a `report` key (only `summary`), so `internal_agent.py:505`'s `result.get("report") or result.get("summary")` always fell through to the terse one-liner summary. Fixed by adding a `_build_report()` method that produces a markdown report with goal, counts, and up to 5 deduped per-step failure details (failure_phase + issues text). This flows through the existing `result.get("report")` path. (3) `tasks/service.py::_apply_result` — on the FAILED path, the code returned before reaching `add_comment`, so the agent_comment was silently dropped. Fixed to post the agent_comment BEFORE transitioning to FAILED. Together these fixes (a) stop mislabeling failed runs as done, and (b) make the next failure self-diagnosing — the real per-step error text will appear in the task's comment. Tests: `tests/test_internal_agent_did_work.py` (12 tests — 1/22→FAIL, 9/10→SUCCESS, 0 steps+long report→SUCCESS, 0 steps+short report→FAIL, BLOCKED→always FAIL, files-changed override), `tests/test_task_service_failed_comment.py` (4 tests — FAILED posts agent_comment, FAILED without comment still fails, FAILED sets error_message, SUCCESS posts comment), `tests/test_agent_runner.py` extended with 4 `_build_report` tests (includes failure issues, dedupes 50 identical failures, capped at 5, no-failures case).
- **★7 Adaptive Loop Halting + MCP structured output support (2026-07-13)**. Two daily-automation improvements aligned with ecosystem trends: (1) **★7 Adaptive Loop Halting** — new `agent/adaptive_halting.py` (`AdaptiveHalter`) provides a velocity/failure-rate gate that operates at the STEP level, complementing the existing `StuckDetector` (tool-loop repetition) and confidence-threshold halt (high-confidence early exit). The halter tracks consecutive step failures and the overall applied-to-attempted ratio; when either crosses a threshold it aborts the remaining steps and logs the reason, preventing further token burn on plans that have stopped converging. Configurable via `AGENT_HALT_CONSECUTIVE_FAILURES` (default 3), `AGENT_HALT_MIN_VELOCITY` (default 0.25), `AGENT_HALT_MIN_STEPS` (default 4). Wired into `AgentRunner.run()` alongside the existing halt mechanisms; reset at the start of each `run()` call so a reused runner instance never carries over state. (2) **MCP structured output (spec 2025-11-25)** — `agent/mcp_client.py` gains `MCPToolResult` dataclass (text + structured + is_error) and `call_tool_structured()` which extracts the `structuredContent` field introduced in MCP spec 2025-11-25. Existing `call_tool()` is unchanged (backward compatible). `list_tools()` already returned full tool descriptors — `outputSchema` fields from MCP 2025-11-25 servers pass through automatically without any change. 28 new tests in `tests/test_daily_automation_2026_07_13.py`. Inspired by Claude Code's smarter auto-mode safety halting (July 2026) and Codex's MCP tool-search improvements (July 2026).

- **Tasks stuck in TODO — never transition to IN_PROGRESS (SQLite enum serialization bug)** (2026-07-13). TaskStore.create() and update() called task.model_dump() which serializes TaskStatus enum values as their repr (e.g. "TaskStatus.TODO") instead of their string value ("todo"). SQLiteStore stores indexed columns via str(doc.get(field, "")), so the status column contained "TaskStatus.TODO" instead of "todo". The dispatcher query WHERE status IN ('todo', 'in_progress') never matched, so list_pending() returned 0 tasks and the dispatcher never picked anything up. Fix: use model_dump(mode="json") which serializes enums as their values. Files: tasks/store.py.

So none of the Llama 4, Gemini 2.5, or latest-Claude model changes actually took effect at runtime; the 42 tests in `tests/test_daily_automation_2026_07_10.py` failed against the real (YAML-driven) values once run. - **Exception detail exposure — `HTTPException(detail=str(exc))` leaked internal error text to clients** (2026-07-11). 31 sites across `backend/server.py`, `backend/v4_api.py`, `proxy.py`, `runtimes/api.py`, `backend/admin_update_task_router.py`, `tasks/api.py`, `webui/router.py`, `workflow/api.py`, and `agents/agile_api.py` returned the raw `str(exc)` of a caught exception as the HTTP response `detail`, potentially exposing internal identifiers, file paths, or implementation details to API clients. Replaced with a generic `"Internal server error"` message; the real exception is still logged server-side where logging already occurred. Recovered from a stale branch (`auto/openclaw-security-fix-20260705`, an automated `openclaw[bot]` fix from 2026-07-05) whose original commit bundled the real fix together with unrelated line-ending churn (`agent/coordinate.py`, ~430 lines of pure CRLF→LF noise) and a 10,520-line generated `bandit-results.json` scan artifact that should never be committed — both excluded here; only the semantic fix was reapplied against current master. New regression test `tests/test_no_exception_detail_leaks.py` guards all 9 files against reintroducing the pattern.
- **Rollout token budget enforcement in AgentRunner (roadmap ★3) + context-pruner test coverage (roadmap ★1)** (2026-07-06). Two completions from the P0 roadmap, aligned with Codex's "configurable rollout token budgets" feature (July 2026) and Claude Code's context-compaction patterns. (1) **Per-session token budget** — `agent/token_budget.py` (`TokenBudget`, `BudgetExceededError`) is now wired into `AgentRunner`: a new `_token_budget: TokenBudget` instance is created per runner; `set_token_budget(session_id, cap)` sets a spend ceiling for a session; the private `_record_tokens(session_id, prompt_tokens, completion_tokens)` helper is called after every LLM API call in `_chat_text()` (all provider paths: universal multi-provider failover, direct Anthropic, and Anthropic-via-headers). At 80% utilisation a `WARNING` is emitted; at 100% `BudgetExceededError` is raised, aborting the run cleanly instead of burning unbounded API credits. Setting `cap=0` (default) keeps the existing unlimited behaviour. - **Model catalog sync — `packages/ai/model_catalog.py` (Unit 8)** (2026-07-11). Advisory-only mirror of the model catalog (`config/models.yaml` + the active BrainConfig) to the DB so external services can query which models are available without re-implementing the catalog loader. Hard constraints (from the UNIT 8 plan): (1) **Flag-gated, default ON.** The `FREELLM_API_MODEL_CATALOG_ENABLED` flag (in `packages/config/settings.py`) defaults to `true`; the `GET /api/catalog/models` endpoint and `POST /api/admin/maintenance/sync-catalog` endpoint are enabled by default. The flag is the rollback lever — set it to `false` to disable. (2) **Advisory-only.** The catalog mirror NEVER changes brain routing — `resolve_component_model()` always reads the in-process catalog + the BrainConfig cache; this module is purely for observability by external services. (3) **Dual-storage.** Mongo primary (`app_settings` collection, doc id `model_catalog`), sqlite mirror (`model_catalog_mirror` table) — same pattern as `brain_config.py`. Either backend failing is non-fatal; the other still serves reads. Falls back to building the catalog in-memory from the loaded YAML + brain config cache when both backends are unavailable. (4) **Never raises.** All public methods swallow exceptions and return safe defaults (empty catalog / None). The mirror document shape: `catalog_version`, `safe_default`, `recommended_priority`, `providers[]` (each with `provider_id`, `display_name`, `tier`, `key_env`, `base_url_env`, `default_base_url`, `role_presets`, `candidates`, `key_present`, `base_url`, `active`), `active_brain` (snapshot of the BrainConfig at mirror time), `mirrored_at`. The `key_present` per-provider flag and the `active_brain` block are the live-derived fields — everything else is a verbatim copy of the catalog. New module: `packages/ai/model_catalog.py` (`ModelCatalogStore`, `CatalogMirror`, `CatalogProviderEntry`, `CatalogActiveBrain`, `get_catalog()`, `sync_catalog()`, `is_catalog_enabled()`, `invalidate_catalog_cache()`). New endpoints in `backend/server.py`: `GET /api/catalog/models` (returns the mirror) + `POST /api/admin/maintenance/sync-catalog` (admin-only, forces a rebuild + persist). New flag in `packages/config/settings.py`: `freellm_api_model_catalog_enabled` (default `true`) + `is_freellm_api_model_catalog_enabled` property. Tests: `tests/test_unit8_model_catalog.py` (25 tests — flag defaults ON, `is_catalog_enabled()` returns True by default + False when env var set to non-`true` value, `_build_in_memory()` returns catalog with all 14 providers, has safe_default + recommended_priority + mirrored_at timestamp, per-provider entry has all expected fields, `key_present` reflects env, ollama key_present always True, `active_brain` empty when cache cold + populated when fresh (with `active=True` on the matching provider), GET /api/catalog/models returns 503 when flag OFF + 200 with catalog when ON, POST sync-catalog requires auth (401) + requires admin (403) + returns 503 when flag OFF + rebuilds when ON, `get_catalog` never raises on storage error (falls back to in-memory build), `sync_catalog` never raises on storage error, catalog mirror does not affect `resolve_component_model()` (advisory-only), `CatalogMirror` has no public write methods).
- **Standing Instructions (§14) — universal agent discipline** (2026-07-11). Added a mandatory trigger→action procedure set to `CLAUDE.md` covering intent reading, decomposition, effort placement, verification, epistemic marking, self-attack, completeness, refusing to guess, delivery order, and the 10 fake-competence patterns, ending with a pre-send gate checklist. Cross-referenced from `AGENTS.md` so every agent tool — Claude, Codex, Cursor, Aider — is bound to it. `generate_context.py`'s `_load_codebase_context()` now carves out §14 verbatim regardless of its general 4000-char CLAUDE.md excerpt, so the autonomous issue-context-generator agent actually receives the Standing Instructions instead of silently truncating before reaching them. All five CRISPY role prompts (`agents/profiles.py` — architect/scout/coder/reviewer/verifier, the production plan→execute→verify loop) now carry a shared one-line pointer to §14, so the autonomous agent fleet is bound to the same discipline as IDE-facing tools, not just documentation. Note: agents already seeded into `agent_definitions` before this change won't pick up the new prompt automatically — the seeder is idempotent-skip-if-exists; a reseed is a separate, deliberate action against live production state.
- **Security Gate false positive — `.bandit` ini key + `.git` worktree inconsistency** (2026-07-11). The Security Gate workflow was failing with "PR introduces new Bandit security alerts (292 > 286)" even though the PR didn't add any new alerts. Root cause: (1) The `.bandit` ini file used the key `exclude_dirs` but bandit's CLI reads the `exclude` key from the ini (via `parse_ini_file()` → `ini_options.get("exclude")`). So the `exclude_dirs` setting was silently ignored — only bandit's default `EXCLUDE` constant (which includes `.git`) was used. (2) bandit's `discover_files` does `if os.path.isdir(path): path = path + "/*"` on each excluded path. When `.git` is a real directory (normal checkout), `.git` becomes `.git/*` which does NOT match `.github/...` as a substring → `.github/` files get scanned. When `.git` is a file (git worktree, used by the Security Gate's base-branch scan), `.git` stays as `.git` which DOES match `.github/...` as a substring → `.github/` files get excluded. This inconsistency meant the base scan (in a worktree) excluded `.github/` files while the PR scan (normal checkout) included them, producing different alert counts for identical file content. Fix: (a) `.bandit` now uses the `exclude` key (not `exclude_dirs`) so the setting is actually applied; (b) `.git` is removed from the `exclude` list — bandit's default EXCLUDE constant already handles it via glob, and listing it explicitly caused the worktree/checkout inconsistency; (c) the Security Gate workflow now uses `git worktree add` for a clean base checkout instead of the fragile `git checkout <base.sha> -- .` which didn't remove PR-only new files. Also added `# nosec B603,B607` to the 3 `subprocess.run(["git", "worktree", ...])` callsites in `runtimes/adapters/internal_agent.py` that were the actual vetted callsites flagged by B603/B607 (constant git argv, list form, no shell) and `# nosec B106` to the `fake_token` test fixtures in `tests/test_ceo_direct_dedup.py`. After the fix: PR=283, base=286 — PR has 3 FEWER alerts than base (the PR removed some stale model ids). The Security Gate now passes.
- **Portfolio intake test failures (Unit 2 regression)** (2026-07-11). Three tests in `tests/test_portfolio_intake.py` were failing on CI: (1) `test_materialize_creates_tasks` — the production filter `i.status in (InitiativeStatus.PROPOSED, InitiativeStatus.APPROVED)` compared plain-string statuses (from the test's `FakeStatus`) against enum values, so every initiative was filtered out → 0 created. Fixed `tasks/portfolio_intake.py::materialize_committed` to normalise status via a `_status_value()` helper that handles both enum and string. (2) `test_materialize_respects_cap` — the test created 10 `FakeInitiative` instances but they all shared the default `initiative_id="abc123"`, so `FakePortfolio`'s dict-of-initiatives collapsed them to 1. Fixed the test to pass unique `initiative_id=f"cap-{i}"` per initiative. (3) `test_materialize_flag_off` — the test set `PORTFOLIO_MATERIALIZE_ENABLED=false` via `monkeypatch.setenv` and tried to clear the lru_cache via `_s._store = None` (a non-existent attribute). The `settings` symbol is bound at module import time so env-var changes don't propagate. Fixed the test to patch the `portfolio_materialize_enabled` attribute on the singleton directly via `monkeypatch.setattr(settings, "portfolio_materialize_enabled", "false")` — the cleanest test seam. All 7 portfolio intake tests now pass.
- **Bandit B324 fix for portfolio source_id SHA1** (2026-07-11). The `portfolio_source_id()` function in `tasks/portfolio_intake.py` used `hashlib.sha1()` for a content-derived dedup fingerprint (NOT a security use). Bandit's B324 rule flagged it as a weak hash. Fixed by passing `usedforsecurity=False` (Python 3.9+) which both silences B324 and uses the faster non-security hash implementation. The fingerprint is still a stable 16-char hex digest — no behaviour change.
- **Catalog propagation to all remaining call sites (Unit 7)** (2026-07-11). UNIT 6 added `resolve_component_model()` and converted the three biggest duplicate preset tables. UNIT 7 finishes the job: every remaining call site that hardcoded model ids now consults the catalog. (1) `router/model_router._default_model()` and `_default_reasoning_model()` — were hardcoded `qwen/qwen2.5-coder-32b-instruct` (NVIDIA) / `deepseek-ai/deepseek-r1` (NVIDIA) / `deepseek-r1:32b` (Ollama) / `qwen3-coder:30b` (Ollama); now call `resolve_component_model("router", role, provider)` so a UI Apply or `config/models.yaml` edit propagates without a redeploy. (2) `agents/profiles._get_defaults()` — was a hardcoded NIM/DeepSeek/Groq/DashScope/Ollama split; now consults `_catalog_defaults()` first (which calls `resolve_component_model("crispy", brain_role, provider)` for each of the 5 CRISPY roles, mapped to the brain's 4 roles via `_CRISPY_TO_BRAIN_ROLE`: architect/scout/coder → executor, reviewer → judge, verifier → verifier — preserves the coder ≠ reviewer asymmetry). Falls back to the legacy `_nvidia_defaults()` table only if the catalog import fails (defensive — never breaks module import). (3) `runtimes/adapters/jcode.py` and `runtimes/adapters/opencode.py` — `__init__` was hardcoded `meta/llama-3.3-70b-instruct` as the default model; now each calls a local `_resolve_default_executor_model(component)` helper that consults `resolve_component_model` with a defensive fallback. (4) `runtimes/adapters/internal_agent._NVIDIA_DEFAULT_MODEL` — was a module-level constant hardcoded to `meta/llama-3.3-70b-instruct`; now derived from `PROVIDER_CANDIDATES["nvidia"][0]` (the catalog preset) at module import time, with the stale value kept only as a defensive `except Exception` fallback. (5) `render.yaml` — removed the `AGENT_PLANNER_MODEL` / `AGENT_EXECUTOR_MODEL` / `AGENT_VERIFIER_MODEL` / `AGENT_JUDGE_MODEL` env vars from all 3 services (web/worker/hermes). The catalog + DB BrainConfig are now the single source of truth; `resolve_component_model()`'s env-var fallback (step 4 in the precedence chain) is kept for backward compat with existing deployments that have these set, but render.yaml no longer pins them. (6) `.env.example` — documented the removal with a pointer to `resolve_component_model()` and `config/models.yaml`. Tests: `tests/test_unit7_catalog_propagation.py` (14 tests — router._default_model uses catalog, returns catalog preset for nvidia/ollama, router._default_reasoning_model returns catalog preset, profiles uses catalog first, profiles._catalog_defaults returns catalog presets, profiles._get_defaults uses catalog not hardcoded fallback, jcode adapter has no inline hardcoded model id, opencode adapter has no inline hardcoded model id, internal_agent._NVIDIA_DEFAULT_MODEL equals catalog first candidate, internal_agent._NVIDIA_DEFAULT_MODEL is not the stale value, render.yaml has no AGENT_*_MODEL env vars, render.yaml documents the UNIT 7 removal, .env.example documents the removal). 296 existing tests across brain/router/crispy/runtime suites still pass.
- **`resolve_component_model()` — single entry point for per-component model resolution (Unit 6)** (2026-07-11). The codebase had three duplicate preset tables that each mirrored `PROVIDER_PRESETS`: `telegram_bot.cmd_setbrain` had a 4-provider inline table, `backend/server._default_agent_role_models` had a hardcoded NIM/Ollama split with stale model ids (`qwen/qwen3-coder-480b-a35b-instruct` and `deepseek-ai/deepseek-v4-pro` were never in the catalog), and `services/brain_failover._PROVIDER_REGISTRY` had a 14-provider table with `default_model`/`models` fields that drifted from the catalog. UNIT 6 deletes these duplicates and replaces them with a single `resolve_component_model(component, role, provider, requested)` function in `packages/ai/brain_config.py`. Precedence: (1) per-call `requested` override, (2) DB-saved BrainConfig model for this role (when the requested provider matches the active primary AND the cache is fresh), (3) catalog preset `PROVIDER_PRESETS[provider][role]`, (4) env var `AGENT_<ROLE>_MODEL` (backward compat), (5) `SAFE_DEFAULT_MODEL`. Never raises. Also added `resolve_component_role_models(component, provider, requested)` convenience wrapper that returns all four roles in one call (used by `telegram_bot.cmd_setbrain` to PATCH all four role models at once). Call-site changes: (1) `telegram_bot.cmd_setbrain` now accepts all 14 catalog providers (was 4), uses `resolve_component_role_models` instead of the inline preset table, and the help text + usage message list the catalog-derived provider set. (2) `backend/server._default_agent_role_models` now consults the catalog via `resolve_component_model` — the stale `qwen/qwen3-coder-480b-a35b-instruct` and `deepseek-ai/deepseek-v4-pro` ids are gone; a UI Apply is now reflected in the wizard defaults without a redeploy. (3) `services/brain_failover._PROVIDER_REGISTRY` now derives `default_model` (first catalog candidate) and `models` (full candidate list) from `PROVIDER_CANDIDATES` at module import time — the registry keeps failover-specific fields (cooldown, name, tier, key_env, base_url_env, default_base_url) but model ids come from the catalog. Tests: `tests/test_unit6_resolve_component_model.py` (18 tests — catalog preset returned when no DB, per-call override wins, DB cache honoured when provider matches, DB cache skipped when provider differs, env var fallback, unknown role/provider returns safe default, "default" role is synonym for executor, resolve_component_role_models returns all four roles, telegram_bot.cmd_setbrain uses catalog with no inline presets, telegram_bot.cmd_setbrain accepts all 14 providers, server._default_agent_role_models uses catalog with no stale model ids, brain_failover._PROVIDER_REGISTRY.default_model matches catalog first candidate, brain_failover._PROVIDER_REGISTRY.models matches catalog candidate list). 125 existing brain-related tests + 104 telegram tests still pass.

Adding a provider to the catalog silently dropped it from the UI. - **Model catalog `config/models.yaml` (Unit 4)** (2026-07-11). New committed YAML file is the single source of truth for per-provider metadata (display name, tier, key/base-url env vars, default base URL), role presets (planner/executor/verifier/judge), and the ordered failover candidate list. `packages/ai/brain_config.py` loads the YAML at module import via `_load_models_yaml()`; the existing hardcoded dicts (`PROVIDER_PRESETS`, `PROVIDER_KEY_ENV`, `PROVIDER_BASE_URL_ENV`, `PROVIDER_DEFAULT_BASE_URL`) are now overridable — when the YAML is present and valid it overrides them in place; when missing or corrupt the module falls back to the in-module defaults so a bad YAML edit can never brick the agent loop. New module-level dicts: `PROVIDER_CANDIDATES` (per-provider ordered failover list), `PROVIDER_DISPLAY_NAMES`, `PROVIDER_TIERS` (free/paid/local). - **Fix duplicate ceo_direct tasks (Unit 1)** (2026-07-11). The self-heal task dedup now has a BACKFILL pass that parses the issue number from legacy task titles (regex `^(issue|quick-note) #(\d+):`) and sets `source_id`, then a DEDUP pass that keeps `in_progress > done > oldest-created` and deletes surplus. - **CI fix: `test_patch_rejects_invalid_provider` used a now-valid provider as its "invalid" example** (2026-07-10). PR #1002's `Test (Python 3.13)` check was red with `assert 200 == 422`. - **Follow-up to #1002: skill descriptions weren't reaching `scripts/ai_runner.py manifest`** (2026-07-10). The 15 skills PR #1002 added `description:` frontmatter to used quoted single-line YAML scalars (`description: "..."`), but all 28 pre-existing skills use the block-scalar form (`description: >` + indented body) — and `scripts/ai_runner.py:cmd_manifest()`'s regex only recognizes the block-scalar form, so those 15 descriptions rendered blank under `python scripts/ai_runner.py manifest` (flagged by an automated PR review after #1002 had already merged). Reformatted all 15 to block-scalar to match the established convention and the manifest parser. Also adds regression tests that were missing for PR #1002's YAML-frontmatter-skip fix: `agent/skill_registry.py::_first_paragraph` and `agent/skills.py::SkillLibrary._extract_description` now each have a test asserting frontmatter doesn't leak through as the description (previously only covered indirectly via the GitHub-registry code path, not the local-skills path these two functions serve).
- **Autonomous self-healing system** (2026-07-09). New `services/self_heal.py` runs a background loop every 5 minutes that automatically fixes four common failure modes without human intervention: (1) **Task dedup** — scans for duplicate tasks (same `source_id` or same `title+source`) and deletes the duplicates, preventing the "tons of duplicate tasks" buildup from the CEO agency creating tasks on every cycle. (2) **Brain failover reset** — when ALL brain providers are unhealthy (all circuit breakers open — the "no healthy providers left" deadlock), resets all breakers to CLOSED and clears cooldown timers so the next LLM call can try again. Without this, the system stays stuck until the longest cooldown expires (up to 10 minutes for 410 Gone). (3) **Stuck task cleanup** — moves tasks that have been IN_PROGRESS for more than 30 minutes back to TODO with `pending_agent_run=True` (they were likely abandoned by a crashed worker). (4) **Telegram webhook clear** — checks and clears any set webhook so the bot's long-polling works. New `POST /api/admin/maintenance/self-heal` endpoint for manual triggers. Configurable via `SELF_HEAL_INTERVAL_SEC` (default 300s) and `STUCK_TASK_TIMEOUT_SEC` (default 1800s). Tests: `tests/test_self_heal_v2.py` (7 tests — brain reset when all unhealthy, brain no-reset when healthy, task dedup by title+source, stuck task cleanup, Telegram no-token skip, full cycle runs, module imports).
- **Cost/usage 500 + MongoDB down on dashboard — local_metrics queries use MongoDB cursor syntax on SQLite** (2026-07-06). The /api/observability/usage, /api/observability/savings, /api/observability/traces, and /api/observability/summary endpoints all used MongoDB-specific cursor syntax (async for doc in cursor, $aggregate pipeline, $gte operator) that fails on SQLite. Also, the /api/health response was missing the mongo field (changed to storage in PR #1000), so the frontend dashboard still showed MongoDB Down even when SQLite was healthy. Fix: (1) _load_local_metrics_since now branches on STORAGE_BACKEND — SQLite loads all docs and filters in Python, MongoDB uses the cursor. (2) observability_summary computes the aggregate in Python on SQLite (no $aggregate support). (3) observability_traces sorts + paginates in Python on SQLite. (4) /api/health now includes mongo as an alias for storage (backward compat) so existing frontend code does not show MongoDB Down. Files: backend/server.py.
- **Nightly regression workflow hardening (follow-up to #994)** (2026-07-09). Two review fixes on top of the self-contained nightly regression change: (1) the generated `E2E_JWT_SECRET` and `E2E_SECRET_KEY` are now masked with `::add-mask::` before being written to `$GITHUB_ENV` (previously only the admin password was masked, so those ephemeral values could surface unmasked in debug/error logs); (2) the "Generate HTML report" step no longer re-invokes `tests/e2e/test_regression.py` — re-running the suite executed its CRUD tests a second time against the same backend, mutating state so the report could diverge from the gated result. The report is now built from the already-captured `/tmp/regression-output.txt`, and the unused `pytest-html` dependency plus the now-redundant `RELAY_BASE_URL`/`ADMIN_*`/`JWT_SECRET`/`SECRET_KEY` env on that step were dropped. Workflow-only change (`.github/workflows/nightly-regression.yml`); no product behaviour affected.
- **Fix flaky `Test (Python 3.13)` CI failure in `test_daily_automation_2026_07_09.py`** (2026-07-09). The `get_current_time` tests used the deprecated `asyncio.get_event_loop().run_until_complete(...)`, which raises `RuntimeError: There is no current event loop` once an earlier test in the suite has closed/cleared the thread's event loop (and always under Python 3.13). The tests passed in isolation but failed in the full `pytest -x` run, turning the required `Test (Python 3.13)` check red on `master`. Switched the four call sites to `asyncio.run(...)`, which is loop-state-independent. Test-only change; no product behaviour affected.
- **Agent time-awareness tool: `get_current_time`** (2026-07-09). Agents can now query the current UTC time directly instead of relying on hallucinated or stale dates embedded in their context. The new `get_current_time` tool is dispatched in `AgentRunner._dispatch_tool` and returns `{ utc, unix_timestamp, date, day_of_week }` — zero external dependencies, no network call, just `datetime.now(timezone.utc)`. Inspired by the Codex July 2026 feature that lets agents receive scheduled UTC time reminders and query current time. Covered by `tests/test_daily_automation_2026_07_09.py` (4 tests: UTC string format, unix timestamp in range, date + day-of-week fields, unsupported tool still raises).
- **Token budget daily reset** (2026-07-09). `TokenBudget` (in `agent/token_budget.py`) now supports `reset_daily()` — clears token counters for all tracked sessions while preserving their caps, and records the reset timestamp for idempotency. Companion method `maybe_auto_reset()` auto-resets when the UTC calendar day has changed since the last reset (safe to call on every request). New proxy endpoint `POST /agent/budget/reset` lets operators reclaim each session's full daily token allocation at the start of a new quota day without losing configured caps. Inspired by Codex rollout-budget reset-credits (July 2026). Covered by `tests/test_daily_automation_2026_07_09.py` (9 tests: counter clear, cap preservation, count accuracy, empty-budget no-op, auto-reset triggers on first call, no-reset on same day, savings report intact post-reset, endpoint 200 + auth rejection).
- **Universal multi-provider brain failover system** (2026-07-07). Permanent solution to the recurring NVIDIA 429/410 rate-limit problem. New `services/brain_failover.py` treats EVERY configured provider as a candidate brain — nvidia, groq, cerebras, zhipu, deepseek, together, dashscope, moonshot (free tier); openrouter, minimax, google, anthropic (paid, opt-in via `ALLOW_PAID_BRAIN=true`); ollama (local). When the active provider returns 429 (rate-limited), 410 (gone), or 5xx (server error), the circuit breaker marks it unhealthy with a cooldown period (90s for nvidia, 30s for others, 10min for 410 gone) and the next call automatically fails over to the next healthy provider. **Model alias mapping** translates the requested model to each provider's equivalent (e.g. `meta/llama-3.3-70b-instruct` → `llama-3.3-70b-versatile` on groq, `llama-3.3-70b` on cerebras). **Intelligent ordering**: free providers tried first (by avg latency), then local, then paid. **Exponential backoff** on consecutive 429s (cooldown doubles up to 4x). **Circuit breaker states**: CLOSED (healthy), OPEN (in cooldown), HALF_OPEN (probe). `agent/loop.py::_chat_text` now loops through providers via `fm.next_provider(exclude=tried)` until one succeeds or all are exhausted — no more single-provider dead-ends. New `GET /api/brain/failover/status` endpoint returns the full health snapshot (provider id, health state, failure count, avg latency, cooldown status — no API keys exposed) for observability. Tests: `tests/test_brain_failover.py` (25 tests — registry building, circuit breaker states, 429/410/5xx handling, exponential backoff, next_provider ordering, model alias mapping, fuzzy model matching, status snapshot, no-key-leak invariant, singleton).
- **In-process WebSocket gateway for iOS control of the agency** (2026-07-06). Replaced the external OpenClaw CLI approach (which required a separate Node.js subprocess that wasn't published to npm) with a **pure-Python WebSocket gateway built directly into FastAPI**. New `services/openclaw_gateway.py` implements the full pairing + command protocol: client connects to `/openclaw/ws`, sends `{"type":"pair","token":"<OPENCLAW_PAIRING_TOKEN>"}`, then sends JSON commands (`chat`, `status`, `list_files`, `read_file`, `ping`) that the gateway routes to the agency backend. Single-connection model (one phone at a time). New `services/openclaw_mobile.py` serves a **mobile web UI at `/mobile`** — a single-page app with a chat interface that auto-pairs via the token from `/api/openclaw/qr`. Open it on iPhone Safari, tap Connect, then "Add to Home Screen" for app-like access. `Dockerfile.backend` reverted to plain `python:3.11-slim` (no Node.js needed — the gateway is in-process). Tests: `tests/test_openclaw_gateway.py` (10 structural tests) + `tests/test_openclaw_endpoints.py` (10 HTTP + WebSocket tests — status, QR, mobile UI HTML, catch-all, wrong-token rejection, correct-token pairing, ping command, unknown command).
- **OpenClaw Gateway as a background subprocess inside the existing web service** (2026-07-06). The OpenClaw Gateway now runs **inside the existing `local-llm-server` web service** (not as a separate service) so it works on the Render free tier. `Dockerfile.backend` installs Node.js + the OpenClaw CLI (`@openclaw/cli`, with a graceful fallback if not yet published to npm); `docker/start_web_with_openclaw.sh` launches the Gateway on `localhost:18789` in the background, then starts uvicorn. The FastAPI app reverse-proxies `/openclaw/{path:path}` → `localhost:18789` so the iOS app pairs against `https://local-llm-server.onrender.com/openclaw`. New endpoints: `GET /api/openclaw/status` (returns `enabled`, `cli_installed`, `gateway_alive`, `gateway_url`, `pairing_token_set`, `qr_payload`, instructions), `GET /api/openclaw/qr` (returns `openclaw://pair?gateway=...&token=...` payload + manual-entry host/path/token). The separate `openclaw-gateway` service from PR #957 is removed (free tier = single service only). `OPENCLAW_*` env vars moved to the existing web service in `render.yaml`. `docs/runbooks/openclaw-setup.md` rewritten for the single-service architecture. Free-tier caveat: no persistent disk → pairing tokens are ephemeral (re-scan QR after each redeploy); `BOT_KEEPALIVE=true` keeps the service awake. Tests: `tests/test_openclaw_gateway.py` (17 structural tests) + `tests/test_openclaw_endpoints.py` (5 HTTP tests — status 200, config snapshot, QR payload, unset-token handling, reverse-proxy 503 when gateway down).
- **Voice worker deps moved out of the web image — new standalone `Dockerfile.voice`** (2026-07-03). `Dockerfile.backend` no longer installs `voice/requirements-livekit.txt` (livekit-agents + onnxruntime/av/numpy, ~600MB installed): the web image never imports them since the in-process worker went opt-in, so they only slowed builds, image pulls, and cold starts. The SAM realtime voice worker now has its own image, `Dockerfile.voice` (python 3.11-slim + libgomp1 for onnxruntime, backend deps for the in-process agency tools, no Chromium/frontend) — build with `docker build -f Dockerfile.voice -t sam-voice .` and run with `docker run --env-file .env sam-voice` on any machine with ~512MB free RAM; the worker dials out to LiveKit Cloud so no inbound networking is needed. Push-to-talk voice is unaffected (`voice/` + gTTS stay in the web image). In-process mode (`SAM_VOICE_IN_PROCESS=true`) now requires re-adding the pip layer to `Dockerfile.backend` (commented lines mark the spot) plus a ≥2GB instance — documented in `docs/SAM_VOICE_LIVEKIT.md` and `render.yaml`. Dockerfile guard tests updated: web image must NOT install the livekit deps, `Dockerfile.voice` must (`tests/test_sam_livekit.py`).
- **OpenHands-inspired agent hardening: stuck detection + microagents** (2026-07-02). Two mechanisms adapted from OpenHands (github.com/OpenHands/OpenHands). (1) **Stuck detection** — new `agent/stuck_detector.py` StuckDetector scans a step's recent observations for three no-progress patterns (the same tool call returning the same result 3× in a row, the same tool call failing 3× in a row, two tool calls alternating A,B,A,B,A,B) and `AgentRunner._execute_step` now checks it at the top of every tool-loop iteration — a stuck step stops calling the LLM, records a `stuck_detector` observation + `stuck_detected` session event, and proceeds to the edit/verify phase instead of burning the remaining 15-call budget repeating itself. (2) **Microagents** — new `agent/microagents.py` implements the OpenHands microagent convention: markdown files with YAML frontmatter under `.openhands/microagents/` in the workspace, where `type: repo` files are always injected into the planner's system prompt and `type: knowledge` files are injected only when one of their `triggers` keywords appears in the task instruction (case-insensitive; triggers shorter than 4 chars require a word boundary so "pr" never fires on "sprint"). Injection happens in `AgentRunner._generate_plan` right after the lessons block, capped at 4000 chars, fail-open. Four starter microagents ship in this repo's `.openhands/microagents/` (repo constitution digest + github/testing/changelog knowledge) and work verbatim in OpenHands and any other tool reading the convention. Covered by `tests/test_stuck_detector.py` (11 tests) + `tests/test_microagents.py` (11 tests).
- **SAM voice worker now runs in-process — fully hands-off realtime voice** (2026-07-02). The LiveKit voice worker no longer needs a separate process: the backend lifespan calls new `voice/sam_livekit_worker.py::start_in_process()`, which runs the LiveKit Agents `Worker` in a daemon thread (own event loop) inside the web service — same single-service pattern as the in-web Telegram bot. Enabled by default via `SAM_VOICE_IN_PROCESS=true` (declared in `render.yaml`), forced off under `TESTING`, and a logged no-op whenever `LIVEKIT_*` env vars or the livekit-agents deps are absent; a worker crash never takes the web process down. `Dockerfile.backend` now installs `voice/requirements-livekit.txt` and — fixing a pre-existing production gap — ships the `voice/` package, which the image never copied, so `/agent/sam/speak` (TTS) and the new `/agent/sam/livekit/*` endpoints silently failed on Render while passing in CI; `gTTS` added to `backend/requirements.txt` so push-to-talk speech synthesis works server-side too. New tests: in-process flag parsing (default/opt-out/TESTING), `start_in_process` no-op paths, and a Dockerfile guard asserting `COPY voice/` + the livekit deps install (`tests/test_sam_livekit.py`, 24 tests total). Docs updated: `docs/SAM_VOICE_LIVEKIT.md` step 3 is now "nothing to run".
- **SAM realtime voice over LiveKit — talk to SAM, SAM talks back (taskmaster-style)** (2026-07-02). Full-duplex hands-free voice control of the agency, modelled on github.com/keithschacht/taskmaster: the dashboard joins a LiveKit room over WebRTC and a Python worker (`voice/sam_livekit_worker.py`, LiveKit Agents) is dispatched into the room running Silero VAD → STT (Deepgram → free Groq Whisper) → SAM LLM with function tools → TTS (ElevenLabs → free Groq PlayAI). SAM's brain is any OpenAI-compatible endpoint — NVIDIA NIM by default, or point `SAM_LLM_BASE_URL` at Hermes (`http://localhost:8100/v1`) or the proxy. Voice tools run in-process against the live agency: `get_agency_status` (schedules/tasks/issues via new public `SamAgent.build_context()`), `list_pending_tasks`, `create_task`. New backend endpoints `GET /agent/sam/livekit/status` + `POST /agent/sam/livekit/token` (PyJWT-minted LiveKit room tokens — no new backend deps); new config module `voice/livekit_config.py` centralizes LIVEKIT_URL/API_KEY/API_SECRET + provider keys; worker deps isolated in `voice/requirements-livekit.txt`. SamVoiceScreen gains a "Start live conversation" mode (dynamic `livekit-client` import, live captions via `lk.transcription` text streams, active-speaker ring states) while the existing push-to-talk flow is unchanged and remains the fallback when LiveKit is unconfigured. Setup guide: `docs/SAM_VOICE_LIVEKIT.md`. Tests: `tests/test_sam_livekit.py` (token claims/TTL/validation, config resolution, endpoint auth + 503/200 paths, worker importability).
- **Learning loop: failed runs now feed lessons into the next plan** (2026-07-02). New `agent/lessons.py` LessonStore persists a deduplicated lesson per failed agent step (failure phase + cause, recurrence counter, SQLite under `.data/`). AgentRunner records lessons at run finalization and the planner injects the top recurring lessons into its system prompt on every new run. Fail open by design: lesson recording or recall can never break a run. Covered by `tests/test_lessons.py` (6 tests). README: dead API docs link fixed to the currently served Render URL, karpathy-guidelines added to the skill table, new Learning loop section documenting the mechanism.
- **Skill: karpathy-guidelines (issue #926)** (2026-07-02). New `.claude/skills/karpathy-guidelines/SKILL.md` adapted from multica-ai/andrej-karpathy-skills (MIT): surface assumptions before coding, minimum code that solves the problem, surgical diffs that trace to the request, verifiable success criteria with no masked verification results. Registered in `services/skill_bindings.py` bound to engineering, backend, frontend, architecture, qa and devops families, with integration notes for issue-context, quick-note and council-review flows.
- **Perf: instant paint on repeat loads + per-screen code splitting** (2026-07-02). ActivationGate now caches a confirmed activation in localStorage and renders the app immediately while revalidating in the background (previously every fresh load blocked on a backend round trip showing a bare spinner — 30s+ on a cold dyno). All V5 screens except Chat converted to React.lazy with a Suspense fallback, so the boot bundle no longer includes all 18 screens; each chunk downloads on first open (18 chunks, ~544KB moved out of the boot path). 100/100 frontend tests pass.
- **UI: V6 depth layer — 3D tilt cards, ambient aurora, tactile click feedback, mobile hardening** (2026-07-02). Added an additive design system to `frontend/src/index.css`: pointer-reactive `.card-3d` tilt with specular sheen (applied to all Dashboard widgets via the shared Widget wrapper), fixed `.fx-aurora` ambient gradient field mounted in AppShell, `.glass` panels (desktop sidebar), `.fx-halo` conic gradient ring, `.fx-rise` staggered entrances, and a violet secondary accent token. Usability: global `button:active` scale press feedback and `:focus-visible` outlines on all interactive elements. Mobile hardening at 767px: 16px input font (kills iOS focus zoom), 42px minimum touch targets, media/pre/code overflow guards, 3D and aurora effects flattened on touch devices to save battery, `prefers-reduced-motion` fully respected. - **V2.0 Modernization Phases 2-8 COMPLETE: real code migration to packages/ via Strangler Fig** (2026-06-28). All 8 phases of the V2.0 modernization program are now complete. **Phase 2 (Provider/Brain)**: moved `provider_router.py` → `packages/ai/router.py` (1496 LOC), `brain_policy.py` → `packages/ai/brain.py` (517 LOC), `services/brain_config_store.py` → `packages/ai/brain_config.py` (692 LOC), `services/brain_watchdog.py` → `packages/ai/watchdog.py` (169 LOC). **Phase 3 (Auth)**: moved `admin_auth.py` → `packages/auth/admin.py` (160 LOC), `social_auth.py` → `packages/auth/oauth.py` (210 LOC), `rbac.py` → `packages/auth/rbac.py` (391 LOC), `services/service_token.py` → `packages/auth/service_token.py` (243 LOC). **Phase 4 (Scheduler)**: moved `agent/scheduler.py` → `packages/scheduler/scheduler.py` (662 LOC), `services/scheduler_store.py` → `packages/scheduler/store.py` (261 LOC). **Phase 5 (Storage)**: moved `db/mongo_store.py` → `packages/storage/mongo.py` (50 LOC), `db/sqlite_store.py` → `packages/storage/sqlite.py` (897 LOC). **Phase 6 (Frontend)**: audited all NAV_ITEMS — `providers` + `admin` correctly adminOnly; audited direct fetch() calls — all 4 remaining are legit (setup wizard, admin portal, doctor runtime health, SSE stream). **Phase 7 (Dead Code)**: removed `remote-admin/` (5 files, 1678 LOC) — old admin SPA replaced by v5 React dashboard, zero references in code. **Phase 8 (Docs)**: added ADR-006 (Strangler Fig shims), ADR-007 (storage duck-typing), `docs/runbooks/v2-modernization.md` (module map + test migration guide + rollback procedure). **Migration strategy**: every moved module leaves a thin backward-compat shim at the old path that re-exports every symbol (public + private) via `from packages.<area>.<module> import *` + a `dir()` loop. Storage modules use `sys.modules` aliasing so `importlib.reload()` and module-level singleton writes (`mod._store = X`) work without test changes. Tests that mutate singletons updated to import the real module: `import packages.ai.brain_config as mod`. All existing imports keep working — zero churn in production code. Verified locally: 296 brain+provider tests, 30 scheduler tests, 48 storage tests, 87 frontend tests all pass. Files: `packages/ai/{router,brain,brain_config,watchdog}.py`, `packages/auth/{admin,oauth,rbac,service_token}.py`, `packages/scheduler/{scheduler,store}.py`, `packages/storage/{mongo,sqlite}.py`, `provider_router.py`, `brain_policy.py`, `services/{brain_config_store,brain_watchdog,scheduler_store,service_token}.py`, `admin_auth.py`, `social_auth.py`, `rbac.py`, `agent/scheduler.py`, `db/__init__.py`, `docs/adr/006-strangler-fig-shims.md`, `docs/adr/007-storage-duck-typing.md`, `docs/runbooks/v2-modernization.md`.

- **V2.0 Modernization Phase 1: repository cleanup + packages/ skeleton + config centralization + provider abstraction + model registry + event bus** (2026-06-28). Started the V2.0 modernization program per the architecture framework (CLAUDE.md + ARCHITECTURE.md + ENGINEERING_STANDARDS.md + REWRITE_PLAN.md). Phase 1 deliverables: (1) **Repository cleanup**: removed 7 stale directories (`scratch/`, `graphify-out/`, `roadmap/`, `config-export/`, `.agent_memory/`, `.Codex/`, `.emergent/`) + 1 dead frontend component (`LoginScreen.jsx`). (2) **packages/ skeleton**: created `packages/{ai,auth,scheduler,orchestration,tasks,storage,events,telemetry,config,security,shared}/` — the target package structure for the modular architecture. (3) **Configuration centralization**: `packages/config/settings.py` — typed `Settings` class that reads ALL env vars in one place. Every module will import `from packages.config import settings` instead of reading `os.environ` directly. (4) **Provider abstraction**: `packages/ai/provider.py` — abstract `Provider` interface with `chat()`, `stream()`, `health()`, `cost()`, `limits()` — every provider will implement this contract. (5) **Model registry**: `packages/ai/registry.py` — centralized `ModelInfo` registry with 4 default models registered (NVIDIA, Cerebras, Groq, Ollama). `best_model_for()` selects the optimal model by capabilities, cost, and priority. (6) **Event bus**: `packages/events/bus.py` — in-process pub/sub with event type constants (`TASK_CREATED`, `PROVIDER_UNAVAILABLE`, `BRAIN_SWITCHED`, etc.). No existing code was modified — all new code is additive. 56 Python tests + 87 frontend tests pass.
- **Architecture framework: CLAUDE.md + ARCHITECTURE.md + ENGINEERING_STANDARDS.md + REWRITE_PLAN.md** (2026-06-28). Created the four-document architecture framework that serves as the permanent operating manual for every AI agent working in this repository. **CLAUDE.md**: master architect operating manual with the Golden Rule ("no user-visible behaviour may change unless explicitly requested"), architectural principles, repository constitution, current architecture bill of materials (628 Python files, 85 JS files, 125 API endpoints, 34 loops, 7+ providers), secrets inventory, and the Architecture Guardian directive. **ARCHITECTURE.md**: target repository structure (apps/ + packages/ + agents/ + skills/ + workflows/), dependency rules (allowed + forbidden), provider abstraction design, configuration architecture (single source of truth), event bus design, scheduler redesign, and migration principles (Strangler Fig pattern). **ENGINEERING_STANDARDS.md**: coding standards (naming, imports, function rules), logging standards (levels + format), security standards (secrets, auth, headers, rate limiting), testing standards (structure + rules + fixtures), CI/CD standards (PR requirements + commit format), performance standards (targets + caching + indexes), and documentation standards. **REWRITE_PLAN.md**: 8-phase migration strategy (Foundation → Providers → Auth → Scheduler → Storage → Frontend → Dead Code → Documentation) with zero-regression policy, characterization test requirements, and current status tracking. No code changes — documentation only.
- **Social login loading feedback: spinner + disabled state on click** (2026-06-28).
